I've uploaded a code repository in the directory . Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
[beta10] OCR retults are broken when containing "
When OCRing VobSub subtitles with PaddleOCR Standalone, lines containing a double quote (`"`) seem to be parsed incorrectly.
More specifically, apostrophes (`'`) after the quote are escaped and become `\'`.

Example:
`" It's raining...`
becomes:
`" It\'s raining...`

I am not sure how this behaves when the line contains two double quotes. I can't find a good sub to test it. 

This may be caused by PaddleOCR using a different string representation when a double quote is present, which Subtitle Edit may not be parsing correctly.

I'm on Windows, if that helps.

</pr_description>

Can you help me implement the necessary changes to the repository so that the requirements specified in the <pr_description> are met?

    private const string TextlineOrientationModelName = "PP-LCNet_x1_0_textline_ori";

    public PaddleOcr()
    {
        Error = string.Empty;
        _paddingOcrPath = Se.PaddleOcrModelsFolder;
        _clsPath = Path.Combine(_paddingOcrPath, "cls");
        _detPath = Path.Combine(_paddingOcrPath, "det");
        _recPath = Path.Combine(_paddingOcrPath, "rec");

        _cancellationToken = new CancellationToken();
    }

    private string GetRecName(string language, string mode)
    {
        string recName;
        if (language == "ch" ||
            language == "chinese_cht" ||
            language == "en" ||
            language == "japan")
        {
            recName = $"PP-OCRv5_{mode}_rec";
        }
        else if (ArabicLanguageCodes.Contains(language))
        {
            recName = "arabic_PP-OCRv3_mobile_rec";
        }
        else if (EslavLanguageCodes.Contains(language))
        {
            recName = "eslav_PP-OCRv5_mobile_rec";
        }
        else if (CyrillicLanguageCodes.Contains(language))
        {
            recName = "cyrillic_PP-OCRv3_mobile_rec";
        }
        else if (DevanagariLanguageCodes.Contains(language))
        {
            recName = "devanagari_PP-OCRv3_mobile_rec";
        }
        else if (language == "korean")
        {
            recName = "korean_PP-OCRv5_mobile_rec";
        }
        else
        {
            recName = "latin_PP-OCRv5_mobile_rec";
        }

        return recName;
    }

    private string GetDetectionName(string language, string mode)
    {
        if (language == "ch" ||
            language == "chinese_cht" ||
            language == "en" ||
            language == "japan" ||
            language == "korean" ||
            LatinLanguageCodes.Contains(language) ||
            EslavLanguageCodes.Contains(language))
        {
            return $"PP-OCRv5_{mode}_det";
        }
        else
        {
            return "PP-OCRv3_mobile_det";
        }
    }

    private static SKBitmap MakeTransparentBlack(SKBitmap bitmap)
    {
        if (bitmap == null)
        {
            throw new ArgumentNullException(nameof(bitmap));
        }

        var workingBitmap = bitmap.IsImmutable
            ? new SKBitmap(bitmap.Width, bitmap.Height, bitmap.ColorType, bitmap.AlphaType)
            : bitmap;

        if (workingBitmap != bitmap)
        {
            using var canvas = new SKCanvas(workingBitmap);
            canvas.DrawBitmap(bitmap, 0, 0);
        }

        // Get all pixels at once
        var colors = workingBitmap.Pixels;
        var blackOpaque = new SKColor(0, 0, 0, 255);

        for (int i = 0; i < colors.Length; i++)
        {
            if (colors[i].Alpha < 100)
            {
                colors[i] = blackOpaque;
            }
        }

        // Set all pixels back at once
        workingBitmap.Pixels = colors;

        return workingBitmap;
    }


    public async Task OcrBatch(OcrEngineType engineType, List<PaddleOcrBatchInput> bitmaps, string language,
        string mode, IProgress<PaddleOcrBatchProgress> progress, CancellationToken cancellationToken)
    {
        string detFilePrefix = MakeDetPrefix(language);
        string recFilePrefix = MakeRecPrefix(language);
        var detName = GetDetectionName(language, mode);
        var recName = GetRecName(language, mode);
        _batchProgress = progress;
        var folder = Path.Combine(Path.GetTempPath(), Guid.NewGuid().ToString());
        Directory.CreateDirectory(folder);
        _batchFileNames = new List<PaddleOcrBatchInput>(bitmaps.Count);

        var batchFileNamesList = new ConcurrentBag<PaddleOcrBatchInput>();

        var parallelOptions = new ParallelOptions
        {
            CancellationToken = cancellationToken,
            MaxDegreeOfParallelism = Environment.ProcessorCount // Adjust as needed
        };

        await Parallel.ForEachAsync(bitmaps, parallelOptions, async (input, ct) =>
        {
            SKBitmap? bitmap = null;
            SKBitmap? borderedBitmap = null;
            try
            {
                bitmap = input.Bitmap?.Copy() ?? new SKBitmap(1, 1, true);
                // bitmap = MakeTransparentBlack(bitmap);
                borderedBitmap = CreateDoubleBorder(bitmap, 10, SKColors.Black, new SKColor(0, 0, 0, 0));
                var tempImage = Path.Combine(folder, input.Index.ToString("0000") + ".png");
                input.FileName = tempImage;
                batchFileNamesList.Add(input);

                using var image = SKImage.FromBitmap(borderedBitmap);
                using var data = image.Encode(SKEncodedImageFormat.Png, 90);
                await File.WriteAllBytesAsync(tempImage, data.ToArray(), ct);
            }
            catch
            {
                // ignore
                return;
            }
            finally
            {
                bitmap?.Dispose();
                borderedBitmap?.Dispose();
            }
        });

        // Add all processed items back to the original collection
        _batchFileNames.AddRange(batchFileNamesList);

        var parameters = $"ocr -i \"{folder}\" " +
                         "--use_textline_orientation true " +
                         "--use_doc_orientation_classify false " +
                         "--use_doc_unwarping false " +
                         $"--lang {language} " +
                         $"--text_detection_model_dir \"{_detPath + Path.DirectorySeparatorChar + detName}\" " +
                         $"--text_detection_model_name \"{detName}\" " +
                         $"--text_recognition_model_dir \"{_recPath + Path.DirectorySeparatorChar + recName}\" " +
                         $"--text_recognition_model_name \"{recName}\" " +
                         $"--textline_orientation_model_dir \"{_clsPath + Path.DirectorySeparatorChar + TextlineOrientationModelName}\" " +
                         $"--textline_orientation_model_name \"{TextlineOrientationModelName}\"";

        var paddleOcrPath = Path.Combine(Se.PaddleOcrFolder, "paddleocr.bin");
        if (engineType != OcrEngineType.PaddleOcrStandalone || !File.Exists(paddleOcrPath))
        {
            paddleOcrPath = "paddleocr";
        }

        if (engineType == OcrEngineType.PaddleOcrStandalone &&
            File.Exists(Path.Combine(Se.PaddleOcrFolder, "paddleocr.exe")))
        {
            paddleOcrPath = Path.Combine(Se.PaddleOcrFolder, "paddleocr.exe");
        }

        if (engineType == OcrEngineType.PaddleOcrPython)
        {
            paddleOcrPath = GetPaddleOcrPytonPath();
        }

        var process = new Process
        {
            StartInfo = new ProcessStartInfo
            {
                FileName = paddleOcrPath,
                Arguments = parameters,
                UseShellExecute = false,
                RedirectStandardOutput = true,
                RedirectStandardError = true,
                CreateNoWindow = true,
            },
        };

        process.StartInfo.StandardOutputEncoding = Encoding.UTF8;
        process.StartInfo.RedirectStandardOutput = true;
        process.StartInfo.EnvironmentVariables["PYTHONIOENCODING"] = "utf-8";
        process.StartInfo.EnvironmentVariables["PYTHONUTF8"] = "1";
        process.OutputDataReceived += OutputHandlerBatch;
        _textDetectionResults.Clear();

#pragma warning disable CA1416 // Validate platform compatibility
        process.Start();
#pragma warning restore CA1416 // Validate platform compatibility;

        process.BeginOutputReadLine();

        await process.WaitForExitAsync(cancellationToken);

        if (process.ExitCode != 0)
        {
            Error = await process.StandardError.ReadToEndAsync(cancellationToken);
            Se.LogError($"PaddleOCR failed with exit code {process.ExitCode} and error: {Error}");
            return;
        }

        if (_textDetectionResults.Count > 0)
        {
            var input = _batchFileNames.First(p => p.FileName == _batchFileName);
            var p = new PaddleOcrBatchProgress
            {
                Index = input.Index,
                Text = MakeResult(_textDetectionResults),
                Item = input.Item,
            };
            _batchProgress?.Report(p);
            _textDetectionResults.Clear();
        }

        try
        {
            Directory.Delete(folder, true);
        }
        catch
        {
            // ignore
        }
    }

    private static string GetPaddleOcrPytonPath()
    {
        var possiblePaths = new[]
        {
            // Windows user install
//            Path.Combine(Environment.GetFolderPath(Environment.SpecialFolder.LocalApplicationData), @"Programs\Python"),

            // Windows pip scripts dir (per environment)
            Path.Combine(Environment.GetFolderPath(Environment.SpecialFolder.UserProfile),
                @"AppData\Local\Programs\Python"),

            // Mac default Frameworks path
            "/Library/Frameworks/Python.framework/Versions",

            // Mac Homebrew path
            "/usr/local/Cellar/python",
            "/opt/homebrew/Cellar/python",

            // Conda default paths
            Path.Combine(Environment.GetFolderPath(Environment.SpecialFolder.UserProfile), "opt", "anaconda3"),
            Path.Combine(Environment.GetFolderPath(Environment.SpecialFolder.UserProfile), "miniconda3")
        };

        string executableName;
        if (Environment.OSVersion.Platform == PlatformID.Win32NT)
        {
            executableName = "paddleocr.exe";
        }
        else
        {
            executableName = "paddleocr"; // Mac/Linux - no .exe
        }

        var foundFiles = possiblePaths
            .Where(Directory.Exists)
            .SelectMany(baseDir => Directory.GetFiles(baseDir, executableName, SearchOption.AllDirectories))
            .ToList();

        if (foundFiles.Any())
        {
            var sitePackages = foundFiles
                .Where(p => p.Contains("site-packages"))
                .OrderByDescending(p => p.Length)
                .ToList();
            if (sitePackages.Any())
            {
                return sitePackages.Last();
            }

            return foundFiles.Last();
        }
        else
        {
            return "paddleocr"; // Fallback to just the command name
        }
    }

    private static SKBitmap CreateDoubleBorder(SKBitmap source, int borderSize, SKColor innerColor, SKColor outerColor)
    {
        var totalBorder = borderSize * 2;
        var finalWidth = source.Width + totalBorder * 2;
        var finalHeight = source.Height + totalBorder * 2;

        var result = new SKBitmap(finalWidth, finalHeight);
        using var canvas = new SKCanvas(result);

        // Clear with outer border color
        canvas.Clear(outerColor);

        // Draw inner border rectangle
        using var paint = new SKPaint { Color = innerColor };
        canvas.DrawRect(borderSize, borderSize,
            finalWidth - borderSize * 2, finalHeight - borderSize * 2, paint);

        // Draw original bitmap in center
        canvas.DrawBitmap(source, totalBorder, totalBorder);

        return result;
    }

    private string MakeRecPrefix(string language)
    {
        var recFilePrefix = language;
        if (LatinLanguageCodes.Contains(language))
        {
            recFilePrefix = $"latin{Path.DirectorySeparatorChar}latin_PP-OCRv3_rec_infer";
        }
        else if (ArabicLanguageCodes.Contains(language))
        {
            recFilePrefix = $"arabic{Path.DirectorySeparatorChar}arabic_PP-OCRv4_rec_infer";
        }
        else if (CyrillicLanguageCodes.Contains(language))
        {
            recFilePrefix = $"cyrillic{Path.DirectorySeparatorChar}cyrillic_PP-OCRv3_rec_infer";
        }
        else if (DevanagariLanguageCodes.Contains(language))
        {
            recFilePrefix = $"devanagari{Path.DirectorySeparatorChar}devanagari_PP-OCRv4_rec_infer";
        }
        else if (language == "chinese_cht")
        {
            recFilePrefix = $"{language}{Path.DirectorySeparatorChar}{language}_PP-OCRv3_rec_infer";
        }
        else
        {
            recFilePrefix = $"{language}{Path.DirectorySeparatorChar}{language}_PP-OCRv4_rec_infer";
        }

        return recFilePrefix;
    }

    private static string MakeDetPrefix(string language)
    {
        var detFilePrefix = language;
        if (language != "en" && language != "ch")
        {
            detFilePrefix = $"ml{Path.DirectorySeparatorChar}Multilingual_PP-OCRv3_det_infer";
        }
        else if (language == "ch")
        {
            detFilePrefix = $"{language}{Path.DirectorySeparatorChar}{language}_PP-OCRv4_det_infer";
        }
        else
        {
            detFilePrefix = $"{language}{Path.DirectorySeparatorChar}{language}_PP-OCRv3_det_infer";
        }

        return detFilePrefix;
    }

    public static SKBitmap AddBorder(SKBitmap originalBitmap, int borderWidth, SKColor color)
    {
        // Calculate new dimensions
        int newWidth = originalBitmap.Width + 2 * borderWidth;
        int newHeight = originalBitmap.Height + 2 * borderWidth;

        // Create a new bitmap with the new dimensions
        SKBitmap borderedBitmap = new(newWidth, newHeight);

        // Create a canvas to draw on the new bitmap
        using (var canvas = new SKCanvas(borderedBitmap))
        {
            // Fill the canvas with a border color (optional)
            var borderColor = color;
            canvas.Clear(borderColor);

            // Draw the original bitmap onto the canvas, offset by the border width
            canvas.DrawBitmap(originalBitmap, borderWidth, borderWidth);
        }

        return borderedBitmap;
    }

    private string MakeResult(List<PaddleOcrResultParser.TextDetectionResult> textDetectionResults)
    {
        var sb = new StringBuilder();
        var lines = MakeLines(textDetectionResults);
        foreach (var line in lines)
        {
            var text = string.Join(' ', line.Select(p => p.Text));
            sb.AppendLine(text);
        }

        return sb.ToString().Trim().Replace(" " + Environment.NewLine, Environment.NewLine);
    }

    private List<List<PaddleOcrResultParser.TextDetectionResult>> MakeLines(
        List<PaddleOcrResultParser.TextDetectionResult> input)
    {
        var result = new List<List<PaddleOcrResultParser.TextDetectionResult>>();
        var heightAverage = input.Average(p => p.BoundingBox.Height);
        var sorted = input.OrderBy(p => p.BoundingBox.Center.Y);
        var line = new List<PaddleOcrResultParser.TextDetectionResult>();
        PaddleOcrResultParser.TextDetectionResult? last = null;
        foreach (var element in sorted)
        {
            if (last == null)
            {
                line.Add(element);
            }
            else
            {
                if (element.BoundingBox.Center.Y > last.BoundingBox.TopLeft.Y + heightAverage)
                {
                    result.Add(line.OrderBy(p => p.BoundingBox.TopLeft.X).ToList());
                    line = new List<PaddleOcrResultParser.TextDetectionResult>();
                }

                line.Add(element);
            }

            last = element;
        }

        if (line.Count > 0)
        {
            result.Add(line.OrderBy(p => p.BoundingBox.TopLeft.X).ToList());
        }

        return result;
    }

    private void OutputHandler(object sendingProcess, DataReceivedEventArgs outLine)
    {
        if (string.IsNullOrWhiteSpace(outLine.Data) || _cancellationToken.IsCancellationRequested)
        {
            return;
        }

        if (!outLine.Data.Contains("ppocr INFO:"))
        {
            return;
        }

        var arr = outLine.Data.Split("ppocr INFO: ");
        if (arr.Length < 2)
        {
            return;
        }

        var data = arr[1];

        string pattern =
            @"\[\[\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+]],\s*\(['""].*['""],\s*\d+\.\d+\)\]";
        var match = Regex.Match(data, pattern);
        if (match.Success)
        {
            var parser = new PaddleOcrResultParser();
            var x = parser.Parse(data);
            _textDetectionResults.Add(x);
        }

        // Example: [[[92.0, 56.0], [735.0, 60.0], [734.0, 118.0], [91.0, 113.0]], ('My mommy always said', 0.9907816052436829)]
    }

    private Lock _lock = new Lock();

    private void OutputHandlerBatch(object sendingProcess, DataReceivedEventArgs outLine)
    {
        if (string.IsNullOrWhiteSpace(outLine.Data) || _cancellationToken.IsCancellationRequested)
        {
            return;
        }

        Se.WriteWhisperLog(outLine.Data);

        if (!outLine.Data.Contains("ppocr INFO:"))
        {
            return;
        }

        lock (_lock)
        {
            foreach (var fileName in _batchFileNames)
            {
                if (outLine.Data.Contains(fileName.FileName))
                {
                    if (_textDetectionResults.Count > 0)
                    {
                        var old = _batchFileNames.First(p => p.FileName == _batchFileName);
                        var progress = new PaddleOcrBatchProgress
                        {
                            Index = old.Index,
                            Item = old.Item,
                            Text = MakeResult(_textDetectionResults),
                        };
                        _textDetectionResults.Clear();
                        _batchProgress?.Report(progress);
                    }

                    _batchFileName = fileName.FileName;
                    return;
                }
            }

            var arr = outLine.Data.Split("ppocr INFO: ");
            if (arr.Length < 2)
            {
                return;
            }

            var data = arr[1];

            string pattern =
                @"\[\[\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+]],\s*\(['""].*['""],\s*\d+\.\d+\)\]";
            var match = Regex.Match(data, pattern);
            if (match.Success)
            {
                var parser = new PaddleOcrResultParser();
                var x = parser.Parse(data);
                _textDetectionResults.Add(x);
            }
        }

        // Example: [[[92.0, 56.0], [735.0, 60.0], [734.0, 118.0], [91.0, 113.0]], ('My mommy always said', 0.9907816052436829)]
    }

﻿using System;
using System.Globalization;
using System.Text.RegularExpressions;

namespace Nikse.SubtitleEdit.Features.Ocr;

public class PaddleOcrResultParser
{
    public class BoundingBox
    {
        public Point TopLeft { get; set; }
        public Point TopRight { get; set; }
        public Point BottomRight { get; set; }
        public Point BottomLeft { get; set; }

        public BoundingBox(Point topLeft, Point topRight, Point bottomRight, Point bottomLeft)
        {
            TopLeft = topLeft;
            TopRight = topRight;
            BottomRight = bottomRight;
            BottomLeft = bottomLeft;
        }

        public double Width => Math.Max(
            Math.Abs(TopRight.X - TopLeft.X),
            Math.Abs(BottomRight.X - BottomLeft.X)
        );

        public double Height => Math.Max(
            Math.Abs(BottomLeft.Y - TopLeft.Y),
            Math.Abs(BottomRight.Y - TopRight.Y)
        );

        public Point Center => new Point(
            (TopLeft.X + TopRight.X + BottomRight.X + BottomLeft.X) / 4,
            (TopLeft.Y + TopRight.Y + BottomRight.Y + BottomLeft.Y) / 4
        );
    }

    public class Point
    {
        public double X { get; set; }
        public double Y { get; set; }

        public Point(double x, double y)
        {
            X = x;
            Y = y;
        }
    }

    public class TextDetectionResult
    {
        public string Text { get; set; } = string.Empty;
        public double Confidence { get; set; }
        public BoundingBox BoundingBox { get; set; } = new BoundingBox(
            topLeft: new Point(0, 0),
            topRight: new Point(0, 0),
            bottomRight: new Point(0, 0),
            bottomLeft: new Point(0, 0)
        );
    }


    public TextDetectionResult Parse(string input)
    {
        // Extract text using regex
        var textMatch = Regex.Match(input, @"\([""'](.*)[""'],");
        var text = textMatch.Groups[1].Value;

        // Extract confidence using regex
        input = input.Replace(" ", string.Empty);
        var confidenceMatch = Regex.Match(input, @"(\d+\.\d+)\)\]$");
        var confidence = double.Parse(confidenceMatch.Groups[1].Value, CultureInfo.InvariantCulture);

        // Extract coordinates using regex
        var coordMatches = Regex.Matches(input, @"\[(\d+\.\d+),(\d+\.\d+)\]");

        var points = new Point[4];
        for (var i = 0; i < 4; i++)
        {
            var match = coordMatches[i];
            points[i] = new Point(
                double.Parse(match.Groups[1].Value, CultureInfo.InvariantCulture),
                double.Parse(match.Groups[2].Value, CultureInfo.InvariantCulture)
            );
        }

        var boundingBox = new BoundingBox(
            topLeft: points[0],
            topRight: points[1],
            bottomRight: points[2],
            bottomLeft: points[3]
        );

        return new TextDetectionResult
        {
            Text = text,
            Confidence = confidence,
            BoundingBox = boundingBox
        };
    }
}

Now I can see the issue clearly. In the `Parse` method:

```csharp
var textMatch = Regex.Match(input, @"\([""'](.*)[""'],");
var text = textMatch.Groups[1].Value;
```

The regex `\([""'](.*)[""'],` matches text inside parentheses that starts with either `"` or `'`. However, the `(.*)` part is greedy and will match too much when there are escaped quotes in the text.

For example, if the input is:
```
[[[92.0, 56.0], [735.0, 60.0], [734.0, 118.0], [91.0, 113.0]], ("\"It\'s raining...", 0.9907816052436829)]
```

The text `"It's raining..."` contains a double quote, which PaddleOCR might represent as `\"It\'s raining...` (with escaped quotes).

Wait, let me think about this more carefully. The PR description says:
- Original: `" It's raining...`
- Becomes: `" It\'s raining...`

So the double quote is kept but the apostrophe gets backslash-escaped. This means the OCR output likely looks like:
```
(" \" It\'s raining...", 0.99)
```

The issue is that when PaddleOCR outputs a string containing a double quote, it may use single quotes to wrap the string and escape the apostrophe. But the regex `\([""'](.*)[""'],` with greedy `.*` could also match incorrectly.

Let me think about what PaddleOCR actually outputs. Looking at the comment in the code:
```
// Example: [[[92.0, 56.0], [735.0, 60.0], [734.0, 118.0], [91.0, 113.0]], ('My mommy always said', 0.9907816052436829)]
```

So the text is wrapped in `('...', confidence)`.

The issue is: when the text contains a double quote, PaddleOCR might output something like:
```
(' " It\'s raining...', 0.99)
```

OR maybe it switches to double quotes:
```
(" \"It's raining...", 0.99)
```

In either case, the regex `\([""'](.*)[""'],` needs to handle escaped characters properly. The greedy `.*` will try to match as much as possible, and the `[""']` will match either `'` or `"`. But when there are escaped quotes inside, it might not work correctly.

Let me create a test script to reproduce this.

2026-05-29 12:30:48,420 - INFO - swea-agent-SubtitleEdit__subtitleedit-10419 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I understand the problem. The `PaddleOcrResultParser.Parse` method uses a regex to extract text from the OCR output. The issue is that when the OCR text contains a double quote (`"`), PaddleOCR may switch its string representation - for example, it might use single quotes to wrap the string and escape inner single quotes (apostrophes) with backslashes.

Let me look at the regex more carefully:

```csharp
var textMatch = Regex.Match(input, @"\([""'](.*)[""'],");
```

This regex matches:
- `\(` - opening parenthesis
- `[""']` - either `"` or `'`
- `(.*)` - any characters (greedy)
- `[""']` - either `"` or `'`
- `,` - comma

The problem with this regex is that when there are escaped characters like `\'` in the text, the `.*` will greedily consume everything, and the final `[""']` might match the wrong quote.

But actually, the more likely issue is that PaddleOCR outputs strings using Python's `str()` or `repr()` representation. When a string contains a double quote, Python's `repr()` will represent it differently - it might use single quotes to wrap the string if it contains double quotes, but then escape single quotes inside.

For example:
- Input text: `" It's raining...`
- Python repr might output: `'" It\'s raining...'` (using single quotes to wrap, escaping the apostrophe)
- Or: `"\" It's raining..."` (using double quotes to wrap, escaping the double quote)

The parser regex `\([""'](.*)[""'],` uses a greedy match `.*` which would still work for the first case, but then the text would contain the backslash-escaped apostrophe: `It\'s`.

Wait, but the PR description says:
- `" It's raining...` becomes `" It\'s raining...`

So the double quote is preserved, but the apostrophe gets backslash-escaped. This suggests that PaddleOCR might be outputting the string with single-quote wrapping (since it contains a double quote), and then the apostrophe gets escaped: `'" It\'s raining...'`.

The regex `\([""'](.*)[""'],` would match this as:
- `(`
- `'`
- `" It\'s raining...`
- `'`
- `,`

And the extracted text would be `" It\'s raining...` (with the backslash still there). The parser doesn't unescape the string!

So the fix should be to unescape the string after extracting it. We need to handle:
1. `\'` → `'`
2. `\"` → `"`
3. `\\` → `\`
4. Other potential escape sequences

Let me verify this by creating a small script to test

🎬 ACTION
cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/test_parser.cs << 'EOF'
using System;
using System.Globalization;
using System.Text.RegularExpressions;

public class TestParser
{
    public static void Main()
    {
        // Simulate the Parse method
        string[] testCases = new string[] {
            // Normal case with single quotes
            "[[[92.0, 56.0], [735.0, 60.0], [734.0, 118.0], [91.0, 113.0]], ('My mommy always said', 0.9907816052436829)]",
            // Case with double quote in text, wrapped in single quotes, apostrophe escaped
            "[[[92.0, 56.0], [735.0, 60.0], [734.0, 118.0], [91.0, 113.0]], ('\" It\\'s raining...', 0.9907816052436829)]",
            // Case with double quotes, wrapped in double quotes
            "[[[92.0, 56.0], [735.0, 60.0], [734.0, 118.0], [91.0, 113.0]], (\"\\\"It's raining...\", 0.9907816052436829)]",
        };

        foreach (var input in testCases)
        {
            Console.WriteLine("Input: " + input);
            
            // Current regex
            var textMatch = Regex.Match(input, @"\([""'](.*)[""'],");
            var text = textMatch.Groups[1].Value;
            Console.WriteLine("Extracted text: [" + text + "]");
            
            // Also check the regex from PaddleOcr.cs for matching
            string pattern = @"\[\[\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+]],\s*\(['""].*['""],\s*\d+\.\d+\)\]";
            var match = Regex.Match(input, pattern);
            Console.WriteLine("Pattern match: " + match.Success);
            
            Console.WriteLine();
        }
    }
}

cd /tmp && dotnet new console -n test_parser -o test_parser && cd test_parser && cat > Program.cs << 'EOF'
using System;
using System.Text.RegularExpressions;

public class TestParser
{
    public static void Main()
    {
        // Simulate the Parse method
        string[] testCases = new string[] {
            // Normal case with single quotes
            "[[[92.0, 56.0], [735.0, 60.0], [734.0, 118.0], [91.0, 113.0]], ('My mommy always said', 0.9907816052436829)]",
            // Case with double quote in text, wrapped in single quotes, apostrophe escaped
            "[[[92.0, 56.0], [735.0, 60.0], [734.0, 118.0], [91.0, 113.0]], ('\" It\\'s raining...', 0.9907816052436829)]",
            // Case with double quotes, wrapped in double quotes  
            "[[[92.0, 56.0], [735.0, 60.0], [734.0, 118.0], [91.0, 113.0]], (\"\\\"It's raining...\", 0.9907816052436829)]",
            // Simple text without quotes
            "[[[92.0, 56.0], [735.0, 60.0], [734.0, 118.0], [91.0, 113.0]], ('Hello World', 0.99)]",
        };

        foreach (var input in testCases)
        {
            Console.WriteLine("Input: " + input);
            
            // Current regex
            var textMatch = Regex.Match(input, @"\([""'](.*)[""'],");
            var text = textMatch.Groups[1].Value;
            Console.WriteLine("Extracted text: [" + text + "]");
            
            // After Regex.Unescape
            var unescaped = Regex.Unescape(text);
            Console.WriteLine("After Unescape: [" + unescaped + "]");
            
            // Also check the regex from PaddleOcr.cs for matching
            string pattern = @"\[\[\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+]],\s*\(['""].*['""],\s*\d+\.\d+\)\]";
            var match = Regex.Match(input, pattern);
            Console.WriteLine("Pattern match: " + match.Success);
            
            Console.WriteLine();
        }
    }
}
EOF

This confirms the issue. As you can see:

1. Test case 2: Input with `'" It\'s raining...'` - the extracted text is `" It\'s raining...` (with backslash before apostrophe). After `Regex.Unescape`, it becomes `" It's raining...` (correct).

2. Test case 3: Input with `"\"It's raining..."` - the extracted text is `\"It's raining...` (with backslash before quote). After `Regex.Unescape`, it becomes `"It's raining...` (correct, but the leading `"` is now part of the text, which might be the actual subtitle text starting with a quote).

The fix is to apply `Regex.Unescape()` to the extracted text in the `Parse` method.

But wait, I need to be careful. `Regex.Unescape` handles standard regex escape sequences like `\n`, `\t`, `\r`, `\\`, `\"`, `\'`, etc. However, looking at the regex in `OutputHandler` and `OutputHandlerBatch`:

```csharp
string pattern =
    @"\[\[\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+]],\s*\(['""].*['""],\s*\d+\.\d+\)\]";
```

This pattern uses `['""].*['""]` which also has a greedy match. But the `Regex.Unescape` should fix the extracted text.

However, I should also consider: is `Regex.Unescape` the right approach? Let me check what Python's string representation looks like. Python's `repr()` escapes:
- `\` → `\\`
- `'` → `\'` (when single-quoted)
- `"` → `\"` (when double-quoted)
- Newline → `\n`
- etc.

`Regex.Unescape` handles: `\a`, `\b`, `\e`, `\f`, `\n`, `\r`, `\t`, `\v`, `\\`, and also `\'`, `\"`, and `\uXXXX`, `\UXXXXXXXX`.

But `Regex.Unescape` also interprets things like `\.` as just `.`, `\+` as `+`, etc. That shouldn't be an issue for subtitle text though.

Actually wait, I need to think more carefully. The text extracted includes the escape sequences that Python added. Using `Regex.Unescape` should handle most common escape sequences. However, there's a subtlety: `Regex.Unescape` treats `\` followed by any character that's not a special regex character as just the character itself. For example, `\X` would become `X`. This might not be correct for all Python escape sequences.

But for the specific case described in the PR (double quotes and apostrophes), `Regex.Unescape` would work correctly:
- `\'` → `'`
- `\"` → `"`

Let me also check if there's an issue with the regex pattern not matching at all. Let me look at the regex pattern more carefully.

The pattern in `OutputHandler` and `OutputHandlerBatch` is:
```
@"\[\[\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+]],\s*\(['""].*['""],\s*\d+\.\d+\)\]"
```

This pattern has `['""].*['""]` which is a greedy match. This could be problematic too. For example, if the text contains both `'` and `"`, the greedy match might match incorrectly.

But the main fix according to the PR is just to unescape the string. Let me apply the fix.

Let me also check if the regex in the `Parse` method also has issues with the greedy match. The `Parse` method uses:
```csharp
var textMatch = Regex.Match(input, @"\([""'](.*)[""'],");
```

This could be problematic if there are multiple quoted strings in the input. But in practice, the input to `Parse` is a single detection result line.

However, there's another issue: if the text contains both a quote character and the closing quote character appears in the text (escaped), the greedy match might still work because the escaped quote would be `\'` or `\"` and the regex looks for `"` or `'` without a preceding backslash. But the current regex doesn't account for that.

Let me improve the regex in `Parse` to handle escaped quotes properly, and also add `Regex.Unescape`.

Let me also check the `OutputHandler` and `OutputHandlerBatch` patterns for the same greedy match issue.

Actually, looking at this more carefully, I think the main issue is in the `Parse` method. The text extraction regex `\([""'](.*)[""'],` uses a greedy `.*` which will still match the entire string correctly because the closing `[""'],` is unique in the input string (the confidence number follows). But when there are escaped quotes in the text, the extracted string contains those escape sequences which need to be unescaped.

Let me also think about edge cases:
1. Text with backslashes that are not escape sequences: e.g., `"C:\path\to\file"` - Python would represent this as `'C:\\path\\to\\file'` and `Regex.Unescape` would turn `\\` back to `\`.
2. Text with newlines: Python would output `\n` and `Regex.Unescape` would turn it into an actual newline character.

These seem correct.

﻿using System;
using System.Globalization;
using System.Text.RegularExpressions;

namespace Nikse.SubtitleEdit.Features.Ocr;

public class PaddleOcrResultParser
{
    public class BoundingBox
    {
        public Point TopLeft { get; set; }
        public Point TopRight { get; set; }
        public Point BottomRight { get; set; }
        public Point BottomLeft { get; set; }

        public BoundingBox(Point topLeft, Point topRight, Point bottomRight, Point bottomLeft)
        {
            TopLeft = topLeft;
            TopRight = topRight;
            BottomRight = bottomRight;
            BottomLeft = bottomLeft;
        }

        public double Width => Math.Max(
            Math.Abs(TopRight.X - TopLeft.X),
            Math.Abs(BottomRight.X - BottomLeft.X)
        );

        public double Height => Math.Max(
            Math.Abs(BottomLeft.Y - TopLeft.Y),
            Math.Abs(BottomRight.Y - TopRight.Y)
        );

        public Point Center => new Point(
            (TopLeft.X + TopRight.X + BottomRight.X + BottomLeft.X) / 4,
            (TopLeft.Y + TopRight.Y + BottomRight.Y + BottomLeft.Y) / 4
        );
    }

    public class Point
    {
        public double X { get; set; }
        public double Y { get; set; }

        public Point(double x, double y)
        {
            X = x;
            Y = y;
        }
    }

    public class TextDetectionResult
    {
        public string Text { get; set; } = string.Empty;
        public double Confidence { get; set; }
        public BoundingBox BoundingBox { get; set; } = new BoundingBox(
            topLeft: new Point(0, 0),
            topRight: new Point(0, 0),
            bottomRight: new Point(0, 0),
            bottomLeft: new Point(0, 0)
        );
    }


    public TextDetectionResult Parse(string input)
    {
        // Extract text using regex
        var textMatch = Regex.Match(input, @"\([""'](.*)[""'],");
        var text = textMatch.Groups[1].Value;

        // Extract confidence using regex
        input = input.Replace(" ", string.Empty);
        var confidenceMatch = Regex.Match(input, @"(\d+\.\d+)\)\]$");
        var confidence = double.Parse(confidenceMatch.Groups[1].Value, CultureInfo.InvariantCulture);

        // Extract coordinates using regex
        var coordMatches = Regex.Matches(input, @"\[(\d+\.\d+),(\d+\.\d+)\]");

        var points = new Point[4];
        for (var i = 0; i < 4; i++)
        {
            var match = coordMatches[i];
            points[i] = new Point(
                double.Parse(match.Groups[1].Value, CultureInfo.InvariantCulture),
                double.Parse(match.Groups[2].Value, CultureInfo.InvariantCulture)
            );
        }

        var boundingBox = new BoundingBox(
            topLeft: points[0],
            topRight: points[1],
            bottomRight: points[2],
            bottomLeft: points[3]
        );

        return new TextDetectionResult
        {
            Text = text,
            Confidence = confidence,
            BoundingBox = boundingBox
        };
    }
}

﻿using System;
using System.Globalization;
using System.Text.RegularExpressions;

namespace Nikse.SubtitleEdit.Features.Ocr;

public class PaddleOcrResultParser
{
    public class BoundingBox
    {
        public Point TopLeft { get; set; }
        public Point TopRight { get; set; }
        public Point BottomRight { get; set; }
        public Point BottomLeft { get; set; }

        public BoundingBox(Point topLeft, Point topRight, Point bottomRight, Point bottomLeft)
        {
            TopLeft = topLeft;
            TopRight = topRight;
            BottomRight = bottomRight;
            BottomLeft = bottomLeft;
        }

        public double Width => Math.Max(
            Math.Abs(TopRight.X - TopLeft.X),
            Math.Abs(BottomRight.X - BottomLeft.X)
        );

        public double Height => Math.Max(
            Math.Abs(BottomLeft.Y - TopLeft.Y),
            Math.Abs(BottomRight.Y - TopRight.Y)
        );

        public Point Center => new Point(
            (TopLeft.X + TopRight.X + BottomRight.X + BottomLeft.X) / 4,
            (TopLeft.Y + TopRight.Y + BottomRight.Y + BottomLeft.Y) / 4
        );
    }

    public class Point
    {
        public double X { get; set; }
        public double Y { get; set; }

        public Point(double x, double y)
        {
            X = x;
            Y = y;
        }
    }

    public class TextDetectionResult
    {
        public string Text { get; set; } = string.Empty;
        public double Confidence { get; set; }
        public BoundingBox BoundingBox { get; set; } = new BoundingBox(
            topLeft: new Point(0, 0),
            topRight: new Point(0, 0),
            bottomRight: new Point(0, 0),
            bottomLeft: new Point(0, 0)
        );
    }


    public TextDetectionResult Parse(string input)
    {
        // Extract text using regex
        var textMatch = Regex.Match(input, @"\([""'](.*)[""'],");
        var text = Regex.Unescape(textMatch.Groups[1].Value);

        // Extract confidence using regex
        input = input.Replace(" ", string.Empty);
        var confidenceMatch = Regex.Match(input, @"(\d+\.\d+)\)\]$");
        var confidence = double.Parse(confidenceMatch.Groups[1].Value, CultureInfo.InvariantCulture);

        // Extract coordinates using regex
        var coordMatches = Regex.Matches(input, @"\[(\d+\.\d+),(\d+\.\d+)\]");

        var points = new Point[4];
        for (var i = 0; i < 4; i++)
        {
            var match = coordMatches[i];
            points[i] = new Point(
                double.Parse(match.Groups[1].Value, CultureInfo.InvariantCulture),
                double.Parse(match.Groups[2].Value, CultureInfo.InvariantCulture)
            );
        }

        var boundingBox = new BoundingBox(
            topLeft: points[0],
            topRight: points[1],
            bottomRight: points[2],
            bottomLeft: points[3]
        );

        return new TextDetectionResult
        {
            Text = text,
            Confidence = confidence,
            BoundingBox = boundingBox
        };
    }
}

The fix is applied. Now let me also consider if there's another issue: the regex pattern in `OutputHandler` and `OutputHandlerBatch` that matches the OCR output line. Let me look at that pattern again:

```csharp
string pattern =
    @"\[\[\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+]],\s*\(['""].*['""],\s*\d+\.\d+\)\]";
```

The `.*` here is also greedy and could potentially cause issues. But since this pattern is used just to check if a line matches (via `Regex.Match` which returns the first match), and the line format is well-structured, the greedy match should still work fine. The pattern matches the entire line from start to end.

However, there's a potential issue: if the text contains a `'` or `"` character that's escaped, like `\'`, the `.*` would still match it, and the closing `['""]` would match the closing quote. But what if the text contains both `'` and `"`? For example:

```
('He said "hello"', 0.99)
```

Here the text is `He said "hello"`. The regex `\(['""].*['""],` would match:
- `(` 
- `'`
- `He said "hello"`
- `'`
- `,`

This works fine because `.*` is greedy and the `['""]` matches `'` after `hello"`. But what if the text is:

```
("He said 'hello'", 0.99)
```

This also works: `.*` matches `He said 'hello'` and `['""]` matches `'`.

But what if there's a case like:
```
('It\'s a "test"', 0.99)
```

The `.*` would match `It\'s a "test"` and `['""]` would match `'`. This works too.

What about:
```
("It's a \"test\"", 0.99)
```

The `.*` would match `It's a \"test\"` and `['""]` would match `"`. Works.

So the greedy `.*` should be fine for the matching pattern. The actual issue is just the unescaping, which I've fixed.

Now let me also think about whether the regex in `Parse` method has the same issue with greedy matching. The Parse method regex is:
```csharp
var textMatch = Regex.Match(input, @"\([""'](.*)[""'],");
```

This is the same pattern. Since `Regex.Match` finds the first match and the input is a single detection result, this should work correctly.

But wait, I should also check if there's an issue with the `OutputHandler` method (non-batch version). Let me look at it again:

```csharp
private void OutputHandler(object sendingProcess, DataReceivedEventArgs outLine)
{
    if (string.IsNullOrWhiteSpace(outLine.Data) || _cancellationToken.IsCancellationRequested)
    {
        return;
    }

    if (!outLine.Data.Contains("ppocr INFO:"))
    {
        return;
    }

    var arr = outLine.Data.Split("ppocr INFO: ");
    if (arr.Length < 2)
    {
        return;
    }

    var data = arr[1];

    string pattern =
        @"\[\[\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+]],\s*\(['""].*['""],\s*\d+\.\d+\)\]";
    var match = Regex.Match(data, pattern);
    if (match.Success)
    {
        var parser = new PaddleOcrResultParser();
        var x = parser.Parse(data);
        _textDetectionResults.Add(x);
    }

    // Example: [[[92.0, 56.0], [735.0, 60.0], [734.0, 118.0], [91.0, 113.0]], ('My mommy always said', 0.9907816052436829)]
}
```

This uses `parser.Parse(data)` which will now have the `Regex.Unescape` fix. Good.

Now let me also think about edge cases with `Regex.Unescape`:

1. `Regex.Unescape("It\\'s")` → `"It's"` ✓
2. `Regex.Unescape("\\\"Hello")` → `"\"Hello"` (backslash then quote → becomes just quote) - This is correct for Python's escaping
3. `Regex.Unescape("C:\\\\path")` → `"C:\path"` ✓
4. `Regex.Unescape("Line1\\nLine2")` → `"Line1\nLine2"` - This would turn `\n` into an actual newline. But in subtitle text, this is probably not common, and if it happens, it's likely intended.

Wait, there is a potential issue with `Regex.Unescape`. Let me check what happens with `\n` in the text.

Actually, looking at the Python PaddleOCR output format: when PaddleOCR outputs text, it uses Python's `repr()` or `str()`. If the text contains a literal backslash followed by 'n', Python would output `\\n` (escaped backslash, then 'n'). `Regex.Unescape` would turn `\\n` into `\n` (backslash + n), which is correct.

If the text contains an actual newline, Python would output `\n` and `Regex.Unescape` would turn it into a newline character. That seems correct too.

But what about `\t` (tab)? Same logic applies.

Now, there's one more thing to consider: the regex pattern in `OutputHandler` and `OutputHandlerBatch` might not match when there are escaped characters. Let me test:

The pattern is:
```
@"\[\[\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+]],\s*\(['""].*['""],\s*\d+\.\d+\)\]"
```

The `.*` portion matches any characters (except newline). So escaped characters like `\'`, `\"`, `\\` would all be matched by `.*`. The closing `['""]` would then match the unescaped quote that closes the string. This should work correctly.

But wait, what if the text contains a backslash followed by the closing quote? For example, if the text ends with a backslash:
```
('text\\', 0.99)
```

Here the text is `text\`. The `.*` would match `text\\` and `['""]` would match `'`. This works.

What if the text is just a backslash?
```
('\\', 0.99)
```

`.*` matches `\\`, `['""]` matches `'`. Works.

I think the fix is solid. Let me now run the existing tests to make sure nothing is broken.

cd /tmp/test_parser && cat > Program.cs << 'EOF'
using System;
using System.Text.RegularExpressions;

public class TestParser
{
    public static void Main()
    {
        string pattern =
            @"\[\[\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+],\s*\[\d+\.\d+,\s*\d+\.\d+]],\s*\(['""].*['""],\s*\d+\.\d+\)\]";
        
        string[] testCases = new string[] {
            // Normal case
            "ppocr INFO: [[[92.0, 56.0], [735.0, 60.0], [734.0, 118.0], [91.0, 113.0]], ('My mommy always said', 0.9907816052436829)]",
            // With escaped apostrophe
            "ppocr INFO: [[[92.0, 56.0], [735.0, 60.0], [734.0, 118.0], [91.0, 113.0]], ('\" It\\'s raining...', 0.9907816052436829)]",
            // With escaped double quote
            "ppocr INFO: [[[92.0, 56.0], [735.0, 60.0], [734.0, 118.0], [91.0, 113.0]], (\"\\\"It's raining...\", 0.9907816052436829)]",
            // With double quote inside single-quoted string
            "ppocr INFO: [[[92.0, 56.0], [735.0, 60.0], [734.0, 118.0], [91.0, 113.0]], ('He said \"hello\"', 0.9907816052436829)]",
            // With single quote inside double-quoted string
            "ppocr INFO: [[[92.0, 56.0], [735.0, 60.0], [734.0, 118.0], [91.0, 113.0]], (\"It's a test\", 0.9907816052436829)]",
        };

        foreach (var testCase in testCases)
        {
            Console.WriteLine("Input: " + testCase);
            
            if (!testCase.Contains("ppocr INFO:"))
            {
                Console.WriteLine("  No ppocr INFO - SKIP");
                continue;
            }
            
            var arr = testCase.Split("ppocr INFO: ");
            if (arr.Length < 2)
            {
                Console.WriteLine("  Bad split - SKIP");
                continue;
            }
            
            var data = arr[1];
            var match = Regex.Match(data, pattern);
            Console.WriteLine("  Pattern match: " + match.Success);
            
            if (match.Success)
            {
                // Simulate Parse
                var textMatch = Regex.Match(data, @"\([""'](.*)[""'],");
                var text = textMatch.Groups[1].Value;
                Console.WriteLine("  Extracted text: [" + text + "]");
                var unescaped = Regex.Unescape(text);
                Console.WriteLine("  After Unescape: [" + unescaped + "]");
            }
            
            Console.WriteLine();
        }
    }
}
EOF

﻿using System;
using System.Globalization;
using System.Text.RegularExpressions;

namespace Nikse.SubtitleEdit.Features.Ocr;

public class PaddleOcrResultParser
{
    public class BoundingBox
    {
        public Point TopLeft { get; set; }
        public Point TopRight { get; set; }
        public Point BottomRight { get; set; }
        public Point BottomLeft { get; set; }

        public BoundingBox(Point topLeft, Point topRight, Point bottomRight, Point bottomLeft)
        {
            TopLeft = topLeft;
            TopRight = topRight;
            BottomRight = bottomRight;
            BottomLeft = bottomLeft;
        }

        public double Width => Math.Max(
            Math.Abs(TopRight.X - TopLeft.X),
            Math.Abs(BottomRight.X - BottomLeft.X)
        );

        public double Height => Math.Max(
            Math.Abs(BottomLeft.Y - TopLeft.Y),
            Math.Abs(BottomRight.Y - TopRight.Y)
        );

        public Point Center => new Point(
            (TopLeft.X + TopRight.X + BottomRight.X + BottomLeft.X) / 4,
            (TopLeft.Y + TopRight.Y + BottomRight.Y + BottomLeft.Y) / 4
        );
    }

    public class Point
    {
        public double X { get; set; }
        public double Y { get; set; }

        public Point(double x, double y)
        {
            X = x;
            Y = y;
        }
    }

    public class TextDetectionResult
    {
        public string Text { get; set; } = string.Empty;
        public double Confidence { get; set; }
        public BoundingBox BoundingBox { get; set; } = new BoundingBox(
            topLeft: new Point(0, 0),
            topRight: new Point(0, 0),
            bottomRight: new Point(0, 0),
            bottomLeft: new Point(0, 0)
        );
    }


    public TextDetectionResult Parse(string input)
    {
        // Extract text using regex
        var textMatch = Regex.Match(input, @"\([""'](.*)[""'],");
        var text = Regex.Unescape(textMatch.Groups[1].Value);

        // Extract confidence using regex
        input = input.Replace(" ", string.Empty);
        var confidenceMatch = Regex.Match(input, @"(\d+\.\d+)\)\]$");
        var confidence = double.Parse(confidenceMatch.Groups[1].Value, CultureInfo.InvariantCulture);

        // Extract coordinates using regex
        var coordMatches = Regex.Matches(input, @"\[(\d+\.\d+),(\d+\.\d+)\]");

        var points = new Point[4];
        for (var i = 0; i < 4; i++)
        {
            var match = coordMatches[i];
            points[i] = new Point(
                double.Parse(match.Groups[1].Value, CultureInfo.InvariantCulture),
                double.Parse(match.Groups[2].Value, CultureInfo.InvariantCulture)
            );
        }

        var boundingBox = new BoundingBox(
            topLeft: points[0],
            topRight: points[1],
            bottomRight: points[2],
            bottomLeft: points[3]
        );

        return new TextDetectionResult
        {
            Text = text,
            Confidence = confidence,
            BoundingBox = boundingBox
        };
    }
}

The fix is in place. Now let me think about edge cases one more time.

One potential issue: `Regex.Unescape` might throw an exception if the input contains invalid escape sequences. For example:
- `\x` where x is not a valid escape character → `Regex.Unescape` will treat it as just `x` (no exception)
- `\u` followed by invalid hex → might throw `ArgumentException`

Let me check how `Regex.Unescape` handles invalid escape sequences. From .NET documentation:
- It throws `ArgumentException` if an invalid escape sequence is found (like `\u` not followed by 4 hex digits).

But in practice, PaddleOCR (Python) would produce valid escape sequences. The only ones we might encounter are:
- `\\` (backslash)
- `\'` (single quote)
- `\"` (double quote)
- `\n` (newline)
- `\t` (tab)
- `\r` (carriage return)
- `\xNN` (hex)
- `\uNNNN` (unicode)
- `\UNNNNNNNN` (unicode 32-bit)

All of these are valid for `Regex.Unescape`. So this should be safe.

Let me also check if there's a possibility that the text contains a literal `\` that is not part of an escape sequence. In Python's `repr()`, a literal backslash is always escaped as `\\`. So `Regex.Unescape` would correctly turn `\\` back to `\`.

I'm confident the fix is correct and minimal. Let me also check if there are any other OCR engines that might have similar issues:

The other changes in `StringExtensions.cs` and `GoogleCloudVisionApi.cs` were already present in the repository before my edit - they\'re not my changes.\n\nLet me summarize what was done:\n\n## Summary\n\nThe issue was that when PaddleOCR Standalone processes VobSub subtitles containing double quotes (`"`), the OCR results were being parsed incorrectly. Specifically, apostrophes (`\'`) after a double quote were being escaped as `\\\'`.\n\n### Root Cause\n\nThe `PaddleOcrResultParser.Parse` method extracts text from PaddleOCR\'s output using a regex. PaddleOCR (being a Python-based tool) outputs strings using Python\'s string representation. When a string contains a double quote, Python may represent it using single quotes with escaped inner single quotes (like `\'" It\\\'s raining...\'`), or using double quotes with escaped inner double quotes (like `"\\"It\'s raining..."`).\n\nThe parser was extracting the raw text including these escape sequences but never unescaping them, resulting in literal backslashes appearing in the final subtitle text.\n\n### Fix\n\nChanged line 69 in `PaddleOcrResultParser.cs` from:\n```csharp\nvar text = textMatch.Groups[1].Value;\n```\nto:\n```csharp\nvar text = Regex.Unescape(textMatch.Groups[1].Value);\n```\n\n`Regex.Unescape` converts escape sequences like `\\\'` → `\'`, `\\"` → `"`, `\\\\` → `\\`, etc., which correctly reverses Python\'s string escaping and produces clean subtitle text.', role='assistant', tool_calls=None, function_call=None, provider_specific_fields={'refusal': None}), provider_specific_fields={'content_filter_results': {}})], usage=Usage(completion_tokens=352, prompt_tokens=35266, total_tokens=35618, completion_tokens_details=None, prompt_tokens_details=None, audio_prompt_tokens=0), service_tier=None, prompt_filter_results=None)
